Shanghai Industrial and Commercial Overview (Continued)

— Compiled by China Credit Bureau

3. Observational Analysis of Changes by Industry

To study the rise and fall of various industries, it is necessary to pay attention to the changing figures between them. Now, the new establishments in various industries for the twenty-third year and the first half of this year are listed in the table below: (Unit: One)

New Establishments　Reorganization　Closure

Year 23　First Half of Year 24　Year 23　First Half of Year 24　Year 23　First Half of Year 24

From the above table, we can see that in recent years, in addition to general industry and commerce, the financial industry has also fallen into the furnace of recession. Other major industries, such as cotton mills, rubber, cigarettes, and flour, are all lifeless. The factories that have reduced work or partially stopped work are not included.

4. Analysis of the Reasons for Changes

It is also quite interesting to study the reasons for changes between industries. Usually, in addition to new establishments, reorganization and closure must have very obvious reasons, such as political reasons, such as wars and government recovery of state-owned enterprises, or general economic reasons, such as market decline, sluggish business, and dumping of foreign goods, or internal pathologies, such as disagreement and fraud. The reasons for the reorganization of various industries and businesses in Shanghai in the 23rd year and the first half of this year are analyzed as follows:

Number of Households in Year 23　Percentage　Number of Households in First Half of Year 24　Percentage

Market Depression and Losses　69　4.96　158　16.65

Financial Difficulties　5　0.34　18　1.90

Internal Disagreement or Fraud　32　2.32　21　2.22

Unwilling to Operate　58　4.23　349　36.78

Shareholders Splitting Shares　6　0.44　157　16.54

Owner's Death or Inability to Manage　71　5.14　68　7.16

Expansion of Scale　19　1.37　7　0.74

Others　18　1.30　8　0.84

Unknown Reason　579　41.90　163　17.17

Total　1383　100　949　100

(Note) The total number of households is higher than the original figure because the reasons for the reorganization of one household often involve more than one. Now, the reasons for the closure of various industries and businesses in Shanghai in the 23rd year and the first half of this year are analyzed again.

Number of Households in Year 23　Percentage　Number of Households in First Half of Year 24　Percentage

Market Depression and Losses　149　35.06　133　49.26

Financial Difficulties　54　12.71　68　25.19

Internal Disagreement and Fraud　28　6.59　11　4.07

Affected by Losses and Closures in Other Industries　14　3.30　3　1.11

Others　19　4.47　3　1.11

Unknown Reason　161　37.87　52　19.26

Total　425 (Note)　100　270 (Note)　100

(Note) The total number of households is higher than the original figure because the reasons for the closure of one household often involve more than one. According to the above two tables, apart from a part of unknown reasons, in the first table, the number of those who are unwilling to operate is the most, followed by market depression and losses, and most of those who are unwilling to operate are due to market depression and difficulty in maintaining, so the two are actually similar. The sum of the two items was 653 in the 23rd year, accounting for 47.19%, and in the first half of the 24th year, there were 507, and the percentage also rose to 53.43. The number of those who reorganized due to expansion of scale was the least, accounting for only 1.37% in the 23rd year, and further decreased to 0.74 in the first half of the 24th year. In the second table, the most numerous is also market depression, followed by financial difficulties. The number of households in the two items in the first half of the 24th year is almost equal to the whole year of the 23rd year, and the percentage has increased sharply from 47.77 to 74.45. In summary, the industrial and commercial situation in Shanghai seems to be still struggling in exhaustion. The way to revival has been discussed by many contemporary sages, and it is not within the scope of this article, so I will not elaborate on it.

Corrigendum: There were errors in the arrangement of numbers in the change table published yesterday. Now, it is corrected as follows: the number of new establishments in September of the 23rd year was 78, not 100; the number of reorganizations in December of the same year was 91, not 15; the number of closures in January and February of the same year was 28 and 27, not 118 and 117.

Educational News

Chairman Chiang Inspects Students in the Capital City and Strictly Orders Correction of Student Uniforms and Living Habits. The Capital City Social Affairs Bureau Immediately Convened a Meeting of School Principals to Discuss Measures.

(Nanjing, 6th dispatch) Chairman Chiang recently inspected the uniforms and living habits of students in various schools in the capital city and believes that they urgently need to be rectified. He sent a letter to Director Wang of the Department of Education, stating that the uniforms and hats of students in various schools in the capital are mostly untidy and unclean. He should strictly order the principals of each school to pay special attention to rectification. When students enter the school for class, each teacher should be responsible for checking and correcting them. In general, hats must be worn straight and clothes must be worn tightly, so as to avoid developing a slack habit. Students wearing yellow uniforms should preferably wear belts to tighten them. He also said that it is not appropriate for middle school students to grow long hair. The rectification will be easier if principals and teachers set an example. It is best for principals and teachers to wear uniforms when they are at school. He also said that the students in the capital lack neatness and seriousness in terms of clothing and actions, and the Social Affairs Bureau and the principals of each school must be instructed to correct them seriously. After receiving the letter, Wang Jiao has instructed the Social Affairs Bureau and principals to formulate strict measures for the rectification of students' clothing system and the revitalization of their daily life and actions, in order to achieve practical improvement, and will urge all schools across the country to pay attention to improvement.

(Nanjing, 6th dispatch) The Social Affairs Bureau of Nanjing City convened a meeting of principals of public and private secondary schools on the 6th to discuss the uniform system of students in the city. It was resolved to form a discussion committee on student uniforms for middle schools in Nanjing City to discuss appropriate clothing styles, colors, and fabrics for reference by the Ministry of Education.

Continuation of Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Fund. Fourth Session of Examination for Studying in the UK.

(Nanjing, 6th dispatch) The Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Fund will continue to hold the fourth session of the examination for studying in the UK, with a quota of 21 students: one for English, one for Western History, two for Law, two for Economics, one for Physics, one for Geophysics, one for Chemistry, two for Geography, one for Biology, one for Mechanical Engineering, one for Civil Engineering, one for Aeronautical Engineering, one for Shipbuilding, and two for Theoretical Medicine. This Year's Compulsory Education Plan in Chahar Province

The following is a summary of the plan for implementing compulsory education in Chahar Province in the 24th year.

Article 1

This plan is formulated in accordance with the outline of the Ministry of Education's Interim Measures for Implementing Compulsory Education and its detailed rules.

Article 2

The implementation of compulsory education in the province shall follow the outline of the interim measures and be divided into three phases. In the first phase (i.e., from August 24 to July 29), all school-age children in the province, in addition to attending ordinary primary schools, should receive one year of short-term primary school education. The implementation plan is as follows: (3) According to the survey in the province last year, there were 205,852 children of school age. Excluding 78,807 who have already attended school, there are 127,045 who have not attended school. It is planned to enable one-fifth of the out-of-school children to attend school each year within the first five years, that is, 25,409 people must receive one year of short-term primary school education each year. (2) According to the number of out-of-school children in the previous item, it is planned to establish short-term primary schools or add classes throughout the province in the 24th year. A. It is planned to establish 125 short-term primary schools throughout the province, each school accommodating 50 children, for a total of 6,250 children. B. It is planned to set up 259 short-term primary school classes attached to the original ordinary primary schools throughout the province, each class accommodating 50 children, for a total of 12,950 children. C. It is planned to expand 127 classes in the original ordinary primary schools throughout the province, each class accommodating 50 children, for a total of 6,350 children. The above three items total 511 schools/classes, accommodating 25,550 children. In addition, the private schools in the province were almost completely banned in the past. It is now planned to order the counties to conduct a detailed survey and order any private schools to be improved within a time limit.

Article 3

According to the provisions of the preceding article, the number of short-term primary schools, classes, and the expansion of ordinary primary school classes to be added in each county in the province, the estimated required funds, and the planning methods: (1) The estimated required funds for adding primary schools throughout the province: A. It costs 120 yuan for each of the 125 short-term primary schools established throughout the province, totaling 15,000 yuan. The recurring expenses for each school are 220 yuan, totaling 27,500 yuan, totaling 42,500 yuan. B. It costs 40 yuan for each of the 259 short-term primary school classes attached to the original ordinary primary schools throughout the province, totaling 10,360 yuan. The recurring expenses for each class are 160 yuan, totaling 41,440 yuan, totaling 51,800 yuan. C. It costs 40 yuan for each of the 127 classes expanded in the original ordinary primary schools throughout the province, totaling 5,080 yuan. The recurring expenses for each class are 160 yuan, totaling 20,320 yuan, totaling 25,400 yuan. The total of the above three items is 119,700 yuan. (2) The compulsory education funds required for the province this year are because the province is both remote and extremely barren. It is planned to implement Article 23, Paragraph 2 of the Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Interim Measures for Compulsory Education, which states that the central government may provide special subsidies for compulsory education expenses in remote and barren provinces. Please subsidize 40% from the central government, 30% from the province, and 30% from the county. (3) The provincial compulsory education funds are planned to be 1% of the total income of the province (according to the budget for the 22nd year, the total income of the province is 3,884,653 yuan, and 1% is 38,846 yuan). (4) The county compulsory education funds are planned to be charged from the following items: A. 3% to 5% is taken from the county's local income; B. Private donations. (5) The central and provincial compulsory education funds will subsidize each county in accordance with the list in Paragraph 2 of this Article, and the amount of funds required by each county will be allocated according to the composition.

Article 4

Each county shall, in accordance with the provisions of Article 9 of the Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Interim Measures for Compulsory Education, delineate primary school districts based on the population of the original villages and towns as the unit for implementing compulsory education and running short-term primary schools. The delineation method is as follows: A. (1) Each primary school district shall be based on an average population of approximately 1,000 people. (2) Each county shall draw a chart when delineating primary school districts, clearly indicating the following items: A. The primary school districts that have established ordinary primary schools; B. The primary school districts that have established private schools; C. The primary school districts that have not established primary schools or private schools; (D) The primary school districts that are expected to establish short-term primary schools this year, and the plan for establishing short-term primary schools year by year in the first phase; (E) The primary school districts that are expected to establish short-term primary school classes attached to the original ordinary primary schools this year; (F) The primary school districts that are expected to expand classes in the original ordinary primary schools this year.

Article 5

In addition to adding short-term primary schools and expanding classes, each county shall also enrich the number of students in each original primary school. The methods are as follows: (1) The number of students in each class shall be an average of 30 to 40 people. (2) For classes with less than 30 people, new students shall be recruited to make up the number. (3) If the number of students in each grade cannot implement a single-type system, a composite-type system shall be adopted. (4) If the original number of students in each primary school has not reached the predetermined standard, the classes shall not be expanded.

Article 6

Each county shall designate a portion of each original primary school to be converted to a two-part system in stages. The methods are as follows: (1) Each county shall designate five original ordinary primary schools to pilot two-part teaching. (2) The primary schools designated for piloting two-part teaching shall be allocated to each primary school district in principle and shall not be compiled in one corner. (3) The primary schools designated for piloting two-part teaching shall be limited to multi-grade primary schools for the time being, and shall be promoted after they are effective. (4) Multi-grade primary schools shall implement two-part teaching starting from the lowest grade. (5) Two-part teaching may adopt a half-day system or a time system, but each class shall be taught for at least three or four hours per day.

Article 7

From the beginning of the first phase of compulsory education in this province, the following methods are planned to be adopted for the reserve of teachers: (1) Each provincial normal school shall set up a short-term primary school teacher training class, and the training period shall be one year. (2) Each county's simple rural normal school shall expand the number of classes. (3) Conduct examinations for primary school teachers.

Article 8

Each county shall select two primary school districts in remote rural areas to set up itinerant teachers and try out itinerant teaching methods.

Article 9

Matters not stipulated in this plan shall be handled in accordance with the Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Interim Measures for Compulsory Education.

Article 10

This plan shall be implemented after being submitted to the Ministry of Education for approval.

Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (87)

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang

Clothes torn, dirty, emaciated, exhausted—it was his awakening—one foot bare, the other bound with an old yellowed tunic, clearly taken from his own back to wrap some wound. He seemed to want to hide behind a haystack, but a unconsciously stretched out arm in his sleep made him discovered. He sighed, mumbled, as if he was having a nightmare, and once he moved, he groaned as if in pain, but he was so sleepy that he soon fell asleep again.

"He shouldn't be sleeping here," said Mrs. Bhaer, and then bent over him and gently called his name. He opened his eyes and looked at her, as if she was also part of a dream, for he smiled hazily and said, "Mother Bhaer, I have returned."

His expression and few words touched her deeply. She reached out to his head, helped him up, and said in her earnest manner:

"I thought you would come back. I'm very happy to see you, Don." At this time, he seemed to have suddenly woken up, and suddenly looked around him, as if he suddenly remembered where he was, and even doubted the earnest welcome. His face changed abruptly, and he said with his old rough spirit:

"I was going to leave tomorrow morning. I only stopped halfway to take a look."

"Why don't you come in, Don? Didn't you hear me calling you? Tandy saw you and shouted to see you."

"I thought you might let me in," he said, already picking up a small bag and turning it over and over, as if he was about to leave immediately.

"You should try," Mrs. Bhaer replied simply, pointing her finger at the door of the house, where the shimmering lights could be seen, as if welcoming distant guests.

Don sighed a long sigh, as if a heavy stone had been dropped from his heart, then picked up a rough stick and began to limp towards the house, suddenly stopping, as if asking:

Sports News

Ministry of Education Sports Committee Standing Committee Decides on Regulations for Selecting Athletes

Must be of Good Character and Excellent Academic Performance and Not Receive Any Preferential Treatment. Severe Punishment Should be Imposed for Any Transgressions.

The Standing Committee of the Sports Committee of the Ministry of Education held its 13th meeting at the Ministry of Education from 9:00 am to 6:00 pm on the 5th. The members present were Zhang Boling, Chu Minyi, Huang Liming, Ling Chen Yingmei, Cheng Dengke, Shen Siliang, Hao Gengsheng, Guan Songsheng, Wu Yunrui, Wu Zheng, Zhang Xinfu, Wang Zhengting, and Yuan Dunli, as well as more than ten people, including Minister of Education Wang Shijie. The meeting was chaired by Hao Gengsheng. The following is a summary of the resolutions:

Resolutions: (1) Request the Ministry of Education to promptly announce the regulations for selecting sports representatives for all levels of schools nationwide. The resolution was passed. (2) How to review the detailed items of physical education for primary and secondary schools. First, the editors Cheng Dengke and Ling Chen Yingmei made a summary report. It was reviewed and approved by all the members, and it was resolved to request the Ministry of Education to promulgate the detailed items and order the education departments and bureaus of each province and city to forward them to primary and secondary schools for unified adoption. If there are any opinions, they can be sent to the association, and the association will consider revising them in the next edition. (3) It was resolved to hold a summer sports school by the Ministry of Education during the summer vacation next year. The purpose is to train physical education teachers in general normal schools across the country. (4) It was resolved to organize a University Sports Curriculum Standards Committee, and the members were determined to be Hao Gengsheng, Wu Zheng, Wu Yunrui, Huang Liming, Ling Chen Yingmei, Yuan Jiaoli, Zhang Huilan, Zhang Jiwu, and Ma John, a total of nine members, who are responsible for forming a letter committee to carry out everything. There were also some minor cases in the temporary motions, which are omitted.

Athlete Qualifications: The following are the five articles of the regulations for selecting sports representatives for all levels of schools nationwide, which were passed at the meeting of the Standing Committee of the Sports Committee of the Ministry of Education on the 5th: (Article 1) Students of each school who are certified by the school and meet the qualifications of the following items may serve as representatives of the school: (1) Those who have good conduct. (2) Those whose academic performance in each subject in the previous semester is passing. (3) Those who are healthy and able to engage in strenuous exercise. (4) Those who have been officially enrolled in the school for more than one year. (Article 2) Those who have committed any of the following items shall not serve as sports representatives of the school: (1) Those who have violated the rules of amateur athletes and lost their qualifications. (2) Those who have been punished by the local sports administrative authority to suspend sports and have not yet completed the term. (3) Those who have violated the regulations for sports athletes of the school and have been disqualified and have not been reinstated. (Article 3) The expenses and uniforms of sports representatives are stipulated as follows: (1) They shall not be exempted from any prescribed fees for serving as sports representatives of the school. (2) They shall not receive any subsidies or treatment for serving as sports representatives of the school. (3) Sports clothing and shoes shall be made of domestic products and shall be prepared by the students themselves in principle. If they are prepared by the school, strict management methods must be formulated separately. (Article 4) A sports representative shall not serve as a representative for two types of ball sports at the same time. (Article 5) Representatives of each school who have transgressions during the competition shall be given appropriate punishment, and those with serious circumstances may be expelled from school.

Yuqing Basketball Team Defeats Xinmin

The Jiangwan Yuqing Middle School basketball team played a friendly match with the Xinmin Middle School basketball team at the school's court yesterday (the 5th). Small Ball Association Seeks Basic Members

The Municipal Small Ball Association will move its address at the end of the month and is seeking 100 basic member teams until the quota is filled. The membership method is that each team only pays a membership fee of one yuan every six months. In addition to enjoying free rental of the ball court, they will also receive a copy of the association's published book "Small Ball Art" and the "Small Ball Weekly" for the whole year.

Corner Dollars Secretly Opened at Eleven Jiao and Nine Fen

Yesterday, the silver industry was mostly calmed after the government reformed the currency system and centralized cash. However, small money merchants in the middle and lower classes were still half-doubtful. Inland neighboring areas, such as big towns, were shipping banknotes to Shanghai for use. Yesterday, it was estimated that another 1.5 to 1.6 million were shipped. However, the market situation announced by the money industry market was generally stable, so the foreign exchange split was still the same. The morning and noon markets were both one jiao and eight fen. The marking and adding water were not counted in the market, and were written off. In the banknote splitting transaction, the morning market had a transfer of more than 3.2 million, the new transaction was more than 400,000, the noon market transaction was more than 200,000, and the small general association had a transaction of more than 300,000. The marking and adding water situation was gradually becoming balanced. There was no news of banknotes being recovered, and the amount issued by exchanging coins and using silver coins totaled no less than six to seven million. In the foreign exchange pledge transaction, more than 400,000 were redeemed, and more than 1.2 million were newly made. It is heard that the loan bank organized by the government will soon be realized, and from then on, the mortgage of real estate can gradually become active. Money shops collected and resolved more than 52 million foreign public bills, more than 3.2 million foreign marking bills, and more than 300,000 from various routes. The banks collected and resolved bills and payments. Yesterday was still the third day of the Western Merchants' horse race, so the customs were still closed in the afternoon. Foreign banks collected and resolved more than 1.4 million bills and payments, more than 3.4 million miscellaneous payments for various goods and exchange pledges, more than 500,000 telegraphic transfers, and more than 400,000 special transfers. Chinese merchants' banks collected and resolved more than 2 million bills and payments, more than 3.6 million miscellaneous payments for various goods and tax pledges, more than 700,000 special transfers, and more than 900,000 telegraphic transfers. Japanese merchants' banks collected and resolved more than 2.3 million bills and payments, more than 2.1 million miscellaneous payments, more than 300,000 telegraphic transfers, and more than 500,000 special transfers. The prices of various auxiliary currency markets were all the same on the surface and had not changed. However, private secret markets were also opened among small money shops. Corner dollars, regardless of single or double corners, were all eleven jiao and nine fen per foreign dollar. Copper coins were stable and unchanged because the overall supply and demand was moderate. The transactions made were generally without a basis, so they could not be calculated. It is observed that the current trend is to reform the currency system, which is an unprecedented event for thousands of years. It is not easy to maintain such a stable market situation now. Therefore, in the future, it will rely on the unanimous support of the financial community and the leaders of the entire commercial field for the government's painstaking reform intentions, and the prosperity of the market will soon be realized. When the market opened in the afternoon, due to the sharp decline in marked flour prices, the issue of currency inflation came to an end. Once the objectives of all parties were revealed, speculators had no opportunity to exploit them. As a result, market sentiment was greatly weakened, and inexperienced long positions were actively liquidated. Near-term contracts fell sharply by 0.10 yuan, and distant-term contracts, such as the March contract, fell by as much as 0.18 yuan. From this observation, it is clear that the frenzied rise a few days ago was indeed driven by speculation. Spot wheat prices, due to the consistent decline in marked flour and wheat prices, also fell by 0.05 yuan. Opening prices were 4.80 yuan for Kaishan East and West Ping wheat, 4.70 yuan for Hankou wheat, and 4.65 yuan for Shaoxing wheat. A total of 3,000 bags were taken by Xinda.

Foreign Buyers and Hoarders Seek to Exit

Northern Ocean Sales Have Weakened... Prices Fall Slightly by 0.20 to 0.60 Yuan

Yesterday, the arrival of foreign xiang rice continued to be abundant, with most of the goods already arriving at the port. However, sales were sluggish. The Northern Ocean syndicate had already handled a large amount of goods in recent days, and their purchase intentions had weakened. Hoarders, seeing the unfavorable situation in all directions, were keen to exit the market at the current price. New purchases stopped, and purchases from Mujie were limited. The market immediately trended downward. The arrival and storage of Wenzhou and Taizhou rice were both abundant, and prices suddenly fell by 0.50 to 0.60 yuan. Other goods fell by 0.20 to 0.30 yuan. A total of 530 bags of Jiangxi rice, 75 bags of Yongbo rice, 2,000 bags of Wenzhou and Taizhou rice, and 500 bags of Hankou rice were sold, all of which were handled by this street. Due to the scarcity of floating storage for foreign rice, hoarders were unwilling to sell at lower prices. However, some merchants and hoarders, unwilling to persist, offered 500 bags of Xiaojiao Saigon No. 1 and Siamese broken rice, with prices falling by about 0.20 yuan each, it was said.

Foreign-Sourced Sesame Falls Again by 0.20 Yuan

Yesterday, foreign-sourced sesame fell again by 0.20 yuan, with 500 tons traded. Contracts were still for delivery in November and December. Yihua handled the import of spot sesame, which remained stable, because it had not risen during the price surge, and foreign-sourced sales were continuous. Therefore, the market was stable. Only small transactions were made by the Eastern Ocean syndicate, with 100 bags of Guandian sesame traded at a price of 8.15 yuan. Soybeans continued to be adjusted upward by 0.05 to 0.13 yuan, and sales to the Nanyang syndicate were quite frequent, with a total of 1,600 to 1,700 bags of various beans traded.

Silk and Tea: Silk Market Maintains Clear and Firm Status Quo

Since the currency reform, commodity prices have generally increased, but the silk industry is the only one that has not seen any changes. The rise in silk prices has already reached its peak, and there is a shortage of raw materials and goods. In addition to the market price remaining high, transactions have not been active. The market atmosphere is clear and firm, as it has always been. The opening of new prices of 900 yuan for white factory silk with 13 to 15 filaments is also as expected.

Core-Extracted Zhenmei Tea Sales Brisk, Prices Firm

Yesterday, the green tea market was not desolate. European firms were particularly interested in core-extracted Zhenmei green tea, because market inventories were low and foreign demand was not weak. Although it was during the autumn racing season, market sentiment remained excited. Yihua, Xiehe, Jinlong, and Tongfu and other foreign firms purchased a total of over 1,100 boxes of Zhenmei, Zhenmei-needle, and other green teas. The spot market price for core-extracted goods was 100 yuan, slightly higher than before. There were no other changes. For Pingshui pearl tea, supply could not meet demand, and merchants were sending personnel to the mountains to search for supplies to meet the needs of foreign firms.

Metals: Reaction After the Sharp Rise in Metals

Yesterday's metals trend showed signs of a reaction after the sharp rise. The reason was the impact of sluggish actual sales. Asking prices for all goods fell across the board. However, the downturn was not significant, so market sentiment was not very panicked. English steel plates (5 mm) opened at 7.50 yuan, down 0.05 yuan, with 170 to 180 dan traded, which were purchased by the Hankou and Yantai syndicates. Black iron sheet and tinplate were traded by both domestic and foreign syndicates yesterday, but market prices had not changed. It was rumored that many new shipments of ribbed steel bars had arrived, weakening market sentiment, and prices fell by 2 yuan, to 117 to 118 yuan per ton, with 30 to 40 tons traded. In addition, there were transactions in all types of metal products, but market prices had not increased or decreased.

According to news from Hankou regarding wood ear, after the implementation of the legal tender, market sentiment turned upward, and most sellers tightened their holdings and refused to sell, waiting for prices to rise. As a result, prices gradually increased. Goods from Hekou and Anyancheng were priced at 90 yuan, and Gucheng ear was priced at 86 yuan. Gao Kui ear was priced as high as 140 yuan. The cottonseed oil market situation had been stagnant for half a month. After the surge in soybean oil prices, factories were unwilling to sell. Traders on this street, seeing the recent activity in oil sales, were keen to add to their holdings. Yesterday, Dayou Factory sold 200 dan, with the price at 16 yuan, a significant increase of 1.50 yuan from before. However, due to slow sales and stable conditions, the market sentiment remained firm. Future developments will depend on sales and the movement of soybean oil.

Shen Bao National Products Weekly

New Monetary Policy and National Goods

— Yang An

The Book of Changes says; 'When things are exhausted, there is change, and with change, there is flow.' Matters of the world cannot escape this principle. Recently, the currency issue has reached a dead end. There are different opinions and diverse theories. The national goods industry has suffered deeply. Recently, the central financial authorities have issued a new monetary policy with swift and decisive measures, and issued a declaration, solemnly explaining that it is a necessary response to the demands of the times and an action that should be taken to reform finance. If it can be used appropriately and managed by capable people, it will not only have no adverse impact on the economy and finance, but also gradually eliminate the panic in China's economy and finance in the future. This policy is very worthy of the unanimous support of the people of the country. However, the new monetary policy has a great impact on China's national goods industry after its promulgation. On the eve of its promulgation, the national goods industry rushed to tell each other to stop shipping goods, believing that the soaring prices in the future would be an inevitable path, and it was also a necessary move to take precautions. As expected, the explicit order was issued early, and prices rose in the evening. The effect of the new monetary policy has the possibility of stimulating price increases. Price increases can greatly circulate domestic goods, giving stagnant industry and commerce the opportunity to develop smoothly. If it is not an excessive rise and avoids the monopoly and manipulation of speculators, it will be sufficient to promote the activity of the national goods industry and be beneficial to the economic recovery of the whole country. Mr. Song Ziwen said, 'Preventing speculation and attempts to excessively raise prices is currently a good opportunity for the government to quickly realize this far-reaching financial reform, and the welfare of the people of the whole country will increase as a result.' This is a very valuable speech. From the standpoint of national goods, the reporter expresses five humble opinions, hoping that the sages in the country will give practical guidance.

1. The legal tender buys and sells foreign exchange without restriction, which has the greatest relationship with international trade. It is hoped that in the operation of foreign exchange business, unnecessary imported goods will be restricted to avoid depriving the original market of national goods.

2. The government and society should promptly pay attention to the stability of the market. To stabilize foreign exchange, it is especially necessary to stabilize prices. Rumors made by petty people and manipulation by unscrupulous merchants should be strictly prohibited to stabilize the market.

3. After the promulgation of the legal tender policy, international trade will inevitably become active, especially export trade, which will have significant progress. It is hoped that the national goods industry will improve manufacturing, refine products, and gain the trust of foreign merchants. In particular, it should study cost reduction and speed up production. Do not just work on raising prices.

4. The legal tender policy is neither inflation nor a low currency policy, but a currency management policy. Therefore, the national goods industry should remain calm and deal with it calmly, be open and honest with the financial industry, seek smooth sales of products, and curb the outflow of money. In particular, it should take a long-term view and focus on the development of foreign trade, so that every point of reduction in foreign goods imported is one point of increase in sales of national goods, so as to revive the declining industrial and commercial enterprises in the country.

5. The biggest pain of the national goods industry in recent years is the depletion of chips, the stagnation of funds, the depression of the rural economy, and the extreme depression of social purchasing power. Since the promulgation of the legal tender policy, not only can funds be supplied to meet the needs of legitimate enterprises in the national goods industry, but also the real estate mortgage law is revised to seek the vitality of real estate. If we are of one heart and one mind and follow the right track, the prosperity of industry and commerce can be predicted, and in the future, import and export trade can have the hope of balance. This is especially one of the most promising points for national goods.

The Legal Tender Policy and the Future of National Goods

— Zhang Zhang

Recently, our Chinese government has done a very meaningful work and issued a very interesting and valuable order, which is the order issued by the Ministry of Finance on the implementation of the legal tender policy, which was published in the newspapers the day before yesterday (November 4). After carefully studying the Ministry of Finance's announcement, the reporter felt that this is not only of great importance to China's national economy and people's livelihood, social economy, and national lifeline, but also has a good impact on the future of national goods. Therefore, I think this is a very gratifying thing. From the standpoint of the national goods industry, I especially feel that this is a very gratifying thing.

According to the announcement of the Ministry of Finance: "Since the drastic changes in silver prices, the phenomenon of domestic currency contraction has been very significant, resulting in the decline of industry and commerce, the depression of all industries, and the outflow of funds, which has greatly harmed the international balance of payments, and the national economy has become increasingly weak. All kinds of bad situations have arisen together. It is estimated that from July to October last year, in the middle of three and a half months, more than 200 million yuan of silver flowed out. If effective measures are not taken, then the domestic cash reserves? There is a danger of being exhausted by outflow!... etc. "After reading this announcement, we can see that the government's emergency promulgation of the legal tender policy is indeed in response to the needs of the environment and contains inherent, epoch-making significance.

Someone asked me, "The implementation of the legal tender policy is certainly closely related to the national economy and people's livelihood. Why does it also have a good impact on the future of national goods?" I think this friend's question is very interesting. We must know that after the implementation of the legal tender policy, the currency in circulation on the market is mostly paper money from the Central Bank, the Bank of Communications, and the Bank of China. Once silver dollars are encountered, they are collected at any time to prevent them from flowing out. In this way, all the cash in the country becomes the property of the state. The exchanges between Chinese people are completely centered on legal tender. If someone wants to smuggle silver out of the country privately, it is actually impossible. Even if they can deceive for a while, once it is found out, it will be confiscated in its entirety. Even if we take the purchase of foreign goods by Chinese people as an example, there was no problem in the past. However, after the implementation of the legal tender system, foreigners need cash transactions. How can they accept your paper money? Therefore, people who want to buy foreign goods naturally have no way, and the products of national goods have a chance to sell well. Isn't this a good thing? Promoting national goods has been shouted for several years, what national goods year, women's national goods year, have all been tried, but in the end, no good results can be obtained. Since the implementation of the legal tender policy, it can be seen that the national goods industry can immediately get an active opportunity. How worthy is this of our joy! Therefore, I feel that the implementation of the legal tender policy has a close relationship with the future of national goods.

Please Students Make a Final Effort to Complete the Work

— Qiu Lang

In the past, the ancients said: "Do not say that you will not learn today, and there will be a tomorrow. Time flies, time will not come again"! These words are deeply encouraging to future generations! Time only rushes forward and never stops temporarily. Like this year, which is called the Student National Goods Year, it has passed quickly and is about to end! There are only a few dozen days left. May I ask how the students have done in promoting national goods in the past half a year or so? I am afraid it is also very ashamed to say! However, the time that has passed cannot be recovered. The most important thing is to seize the present. Please all the students in the country, in these short dozens of days, make a final effort to do the patriotic work of persuading the use of national goods.

Someone retorted to me: "You are too meaningless, the year is almost over, and you are still talking about this kind of nonsense!" I said: No! To put it humorously, take the 10,000-meter race as an analogy; it doesn't matter if you are behind when you run 6,000 to 7,000 meters. The most important thing is that when you are approaching 9,000 meters to the finish line, if you can courageously and quickly catch up, the championship still belongs to you! Therefore, everything is always based on the end result. Moreover, the weather is changing from cool to cold, and the people's demand for food, drink, and clothing is not as simple as in summer. They must purchase a large amount to meet their needs. This is the time when you students are working hard. On the one hand, persuade the people to use national goods consistently. On the other hand, organize investigation teams to carefully check national goods that are mixed with fake ones, and guide the people on the trademarks and forms of various national goods, so that the people can have a deep understanding and will not mistakenly purchase counterfeit products. If you do this diligently, even in a short period of time, I am sure you will get good results, build the final miracle, and complete all the work of the Student National Goods Year.

Women and the Promotion of National Goods

— Yu Ke

A big word 'poverty' has thoroughly penetrated our entire China, but why is it so poor? Natural and man-made disasters in recent years are certainly one reason for poverty, but the biggest reason is still the underdevelopment of agriculture, industry, and commerce. Under the oppression of imperialist economic aggression, the agriculture, industry, and commerce of our country will only sooner or later embark on the road to death. If we want to get rid of this death, we can naturally only abolish the unequal treaties; however, there is another important task, which is to build up agriculture, industry, and commerce. Therefore, promoting national goods is a very important method.

Agriculture, industry, and commerce are interdependent. Without the development of industry, agriculture will not develop, and commerce will not develop. With the development of commerce, agriculture and industry will also develop. It has a causal chain; if we want to develop industry and commerce, we must first make our own industrial products sell well? Commerce becomes our own commerce, and the first step is to prevent Chinese money from flowing to foreign countries; if we want to prevent money from flowing abroad, we must vigorously promote national goods, exclude foreign goods, and make our own national goods sell well, so that agriculture, industry, and commerce can be revitalized, and the poverty of the country can be broken!

This is certain, especially women are most fond of using foreign goods; women like to be beautiful and love fashion. We only need to see that the foreign goods in various companies and stores are mostly women's supplies, and clothing and cosmetics are the largest. There are countless other things related to women. Suppose women can suddenly realize that everyone uses national goods, and foreign goods can almost be cut off and disappear. Female compatriots are one of the people of the country, and they have the rights to be enjoyed and the obligations to be fulfilled; in other words: women have the responsibility to promote national goods and save the country. Otherwise, if the country is destroyed, oppressed, and made a slave, there will be no distinction between men and women! But how do women promote national goods? Briefly describe it below:

A. Promote thrift and purchase national goods:

(1) All women's clothing, accessories, and supplies must be purchased with national goods; and widely persuade family and friends to purchase national goods in a practical way.

(2) Women's clothing should be simple and elegant, and all foreign costumes and excessively gorgeous and valuable items should be discarded.

B. Promote women's occupations:

(1) Promote women to engage in practical operations and not be leisurely and idle.

(2) Encourage women's home crafts.

(3) Organize women's supplies national goods consumer cooperatives.

C. Educate children to develop the habit of purchasing national goods:

(1) Children's toys should be purchased with national goods.

(2) Children should be instilled with knowledge of patriotism and purchasing national goods.

Transforming Psychology

— Yiyi Guanzhu

In recent years, many things in "foreign goods" are now available in "national goods." Moreover, some "national goods" are even better than "foreign goods," and the price is sometimes cheaper than "foreign goods." However, most Chinese people still like to use "foreign goods" and do not like to use "national goods!" Someone asked me: What is the reason for this? I said: This is a kind of psychology, playing tricks there!

Because, in everyone's mind, they think that "foreign goods" are good and good, even if the price is expensive, they will buy it. As for "national goods," it always seems to be crude and unbearable, even if the price is cheap and the quality is good, they are regarded as worthless! Alas! Everyone has this kind of psychology, how can "national goods" raise their heads?

Therefore, I want to use the four words "transforming psychology" as the title of this article. The intention is nothing more than to hope that Chinese people will quickly transform this psychology of loving "foreign goods" and not loving "national goods" from now on. To put it bluntly, it is to hope that everyone will quickly treat "national goods" with the psychology of treating "foreign goods." If everyone can really do this, "foreign goods" will definitely fall without being attacked, and "national goods" can raise their heads. If you don't believe me, everyone may as well try it.

On the Training of Shop Assistants

— Ye Yiyi

—The training of shop assistants is closely related to the sales of national goods—

I have the following fragments of facts as the motivation for writing this article:

Because the school has not been in session for a long time, and various school supplies are not yet fully prepared, therefore, taking advantage of the weekend holidays, I went outside to buy some things. First, I ran to Simma Road, to a bookstore that sells slogan charts. I saw several shop assistants chatting idly. They were wearing beautiful and foreign clothes, and they didn't seem to care about business. After I went in, I looked at the charts and asked about the price; but the upper bodies of several shop assistants were lying on the glass panel and chatting again. When I saw the situation was like this, and the price was also very expensive, I walked out. Along Simma Road to the west, I arrived at Fujian Road and stepped into a paper shop. I wanted to buy some maobian paper to ask my children to bind their own notebooks for practicing writing; but when I asked him the price, a phone call came to the shop assistant, so he left me, this customer, aside and went away; I asked another shop assistant, but the other shop assistant ignored me and turned his head away, probably because this business was not taken by him, so it didn't matter: I waited for more than a quarter of an hour before I bought the paper and went back. After passing through Penglai Market, I went to a shop to buy a Great Wall brand thermos. I went in and looked at several styles. When I was asking about the price, several female customers came. The shop assistant saw that I was asking about the price, maybe it was too troublesome and annoying, so he asked me arrogantly: "Hey! Do you want to buy it or not?" I didn't get angry when I heard this question. I said leisurely: "Of course! I want to buy it. Maybe something happened to your husband? Then, you can ask another shop assistant to replace you!" He was silent, so I chose one for one and a half yuan, gave him the money, took an invoice without a stamp, and left.

Based on the above facts, I personally feel that the training of shop assistants is indeed a very important issue that deserves attention. Because this issue affects the sales of national goods, its relationship is really important and big, and very close. If the training of shop assistants is poor, on the surface, it is certainly a loss for the boss and shareholders; but in reality, it is also a direct loss for national goods and industrial products. Conversely, if the shop assistant's attitude is sincere, his language is kind, his clothing is simple, and his manners are appropriate, the customer will naturally be satisfied and buy, and come again next time after leaving; in this way, the development of business can be expected.

Therefore, the training of shop assistants has a very deep relationship with the sales of national goods; therefore, the training of shop assistants is indeed an issue that should be paid attention to by colleagues in the national goods industry. Now I will briefly write down a few goals of training based on my limited knowledge:

(1) The attitude should be sincere. A shop assistant's attitude is very important to customers; a sincere attitude can make customers feel so moved that they feel like it is very unreasonable not to buy something. Conversely, if the attitude is arrogant, then the customer will look at it and leave, because it can also be bought elsewhere.

(2) The language should be fluent. If the language is not fluent, it is often offensive to customers. For example, when a customer comes, the shop assistant must try his best to introduce the national goods and very politely explain its advantages.

(3) The manners should be respectful. A customer's visit is a good phenomenon, so you should treat him with very respectful manners; if you ignore him and let him look at it, that would be terrible. When he comes, you should treat him very respectfully. You must know that being polite is not a shameless thing!

(4) The clothing should be simple. At first glance, a shop assistant's clothing seems unimportant; in reality, it should also be simple. Because being covered in imported goods is not a model shop assistant.

Whether the above four points are appropriate or not, I hope that readers will give me some pointers.

National Goods Small Toys

— Rong Yu

I introduced the clay sculptures of Huishan as national goods small toys the day before yesterday; recently, I traveled to Suzhou and found something worth introducing, which is the wooden toys produced in Mudu Town.

Mudu Town is more than 20 miles away from Suzhou City. There are good scenery such as Lingyan Mountain and Tianping Mountain, so there are quite a few people who go to play. In the past, traveling by boat took half a day to go back and forth. Now there are highways, and public buses can arrive in less than an hour, so it is even more lively. Since I had already arrived in Suzhou, I naturally went to enjoy it. The red trees on the mountainside and the wildflowers on both banks have a kind of scenery, which is not related to this article, so there is no need to describe it in detail. In Lingyan Mountain and Tianping Mountain, I found many villagers selling some wooden small toys, which suddenly moved my heart. These wooden toys, when I was a child, were also popular all over the country with the big A Fu of Wuxi: I also liked to play with them when I was a child. Unexpectedly, they are now defeated by imported toys and hiding at the foot of the mountain, only for people who visit the mountain to buy as souvenirs. Do you think it is pitiful or not! I looked at its types and manufacturing methods again, and it was much more advanced than when I was a child. The types include wooden eggs, wooden bullets, candlesticks, teacups, wine glasses, rice bowls, vases, pen holders, jars, small bowls, etc., and the styles are also small and exquisite, and the colors are smooth and elegant. If they were placed in the windows of large companies, they would definitely be able to sell at a good price, but unfortunately they fell into the hands of the villagers, and the highest price is less than five cents a piece. Do you think it is miserable or not!

I spent four dimes from an old hawker and bought more than a dozen pieces, and incidentally asked him about his manufacturing method. He said: "The raw materials for this kind of woodenware are made of hard elm wood. Because the large pieces of elm wood have already been made into household utensils, the sawed-off edges and corners have no use, so we buy them by the pound, and first dry them in the sun, because the things made of wet wood will split when they are dry, then all the previous efforts will be abandoned and it will be difficult to change money: After the wood is dried, draw the shape with an ink line, and use a knife to chisel it into a rough blank: then put it on a wood lathe and it will be smooth and delicate! If you want the color to be oily and moist, then apply a layer of cooked oil. Although the capital to make these things is not large, the effort is very costly." After listening to him, I thought that what kind of Chinese handicraft products are not like this! To improve production, we must first pay attention to machinery.

Back in Shanghai, I gave these small wooden objects to relatives and friends, and everyone praised them, so I wrote this article to promote and introduce them.

First-Rank Lady

— Ai Wu

"First-Rank Lady" This is an honorary title of the imperial era, only prime ministers and ministers can receive this title. Although there is no imperial title now, the title "lady" is very popular.

Judging grades by official ranks is autocratic and unreasonable; however, dividing high and low by character is worthy of people's agreement. For example, calling Mr. Gu's wife "First-Rank Lady" is appropriate.

Mrs. Gu has considerable knowledge and is good at cooking and sewing. Since she married Mr. Gu, she has been a good help to Mr. Gu. She helps her husband handle household chores; whether it is guests who have been to her house or her neighbors, they all praise her for her wisdom.

Mrs. Gu's appearance is also very beautiful. According to her, she pays attention to the beauty of her appearance and also takes care of the beauty of her heart, because the heart and the appearance are related. As for the cosmetics she uses, they are also very simple, only two or three kinds, and they are all national goods. She often says to people that it is our duty to promote national goods, let alone this kind of product is beautiful in quality and cheap in price.

Like Mrs. Gu, a woman with knowledge, skills, virtue, and a patriotic spirit, we call her First-Rank Lady. Who says it is inappropriate?

The Invention of Synthetic Gasoline

— Xiang Xian

In the 20th century world, gasoline is a very important driving force, but all kinds of gasoline used in our country rely on imports. According to the customs report book of the 22nd year, the total number of gasoline imports was 21,329,000 yuan, and the total amount of gasoline imports in the 23rd year was 19,312,000 yuan. This year, the development of highways is progressing very actively, and the transportation vehicles that are related to it will of course be purchased in large quantities, then the consumption of gasoline should exceed the previous amount. How can we imagine going on like this? The invention of self-made gasoline by Chinese people is really a matter of urgency. Recently, Mr. Xu Boyun, director of the research department of Hangzhou Minsheng Manufacturing Plant, invented a kind of synthetic gasoline, which has been tested by the aviation school. The results are excellent and are a great contribution to the Chinese people, which is of great importance to the future of the nation. Now I will write down the process of his invention to tell the readers, hoping that everyone will pay deep attention to it.

Mr. Xu Boyun is from Shangyu, Zhejiang, and is 29 years old this year. He studied medicine at Chiba Medical University in Japan and obtained a bachelor's degree. He returned to China in the 21st year of the Republic of China and served as the director of the research department of Minsheng Plant. He is always diligent in the laboratory, engaged in chemical experiments. He has also invented pharmaceutical products such as Daitanling and Ximeiling. This time, the invention of synthetic gasoline was indeed discovered accidentally and unintentionally. It was discovered occasionally from a special type of mineral soil in the hands of a villager, so he engaged in researching its properties and effects, so he learned that this type of mineral soil has a special and good effect in chemistry. That is, when it is catalytically decomposed, it produces very little gas and produces a large amount of oil tar, which is light yellow in color and has fluorescence, which is better than the dark brown oil tar obtained by dry distillation of oil. Therefore, he refined it with the ordinary method of refining gasoline, and then checked its various chemical and physical properties and conditions, and proved that the gasoline refined in this way has the same properties as natural gasoline. Therefore, with the commendation and support of Principal Zhou of the Central Aviation School and Director Zeng of the Construction Department of Zhejiang Province, it was tested on a 120-horsepower aircraft engine on December 15 last year. The test results were better than natural gasoline. This unexpected harvest cannot be regarded as a great contribution, not to mention that domestic gasoline is an urgent need at present. I earnestly hope that the government authorities and the general public will promote and assist it, so that we can release a ray of light for the future of Chinese industry!

Publishing industry

Publishing and the Military

— Xie Bingwen

Publishing and the military, in our China, are as distant as the North and South Poles.

Publishers do business, believing that libraries and schools are their major clients; they print books for professors, students, and general intellectuals. As for soldiers, everyone generally believes that they don't need books besides holding guns. As for ordinary soldiers, they are not only ignored by publishers, but also, in fact, have been excluded from the circle of culture since ancient times. This traditional separation has led to the backwardness of the Chinese military, making ordinary soldiers extremely ignorant and crude. Obviously, this is due to the lack of cultural education in the military. However, the reason for this lack is not that people in the barracks dislike reading or are averse to cultural education; rather, it is that Chinese scholar-officials have historically held the prejudice that military men only need to learn skills and do not need to understand literature. Therefore, people proficient in both literary and military arts were very rare in the past, and the widespread illiteracy in the military is still a very common phenomenon today.

However, the world is evolving. The last century was the 20th century. The boundaries between literary and military affairs have been destroyed by the fierce winds of science and technology. Soldiers using modern weapons must not only arm their hands and bodies, but also fully arm their minds.

For example, the strength and civilization of Europe, America, and Japan are obviously due to the close relationship between publishing and the military. It is said that soldiers' reading materials published in Japan each year account for more than 20% of the total number of publications in the country. Although there are no statistics on the number of pamphlets on military affairs, politics, and economics compiled for soldiers, there are more than forty types of popular magazines for the military alone. In countries such as England and France, many literary figures write works depicting war and military life, and their main target audience is in the barracks. Many soldiers are ardent supporters of Remarque, Rousseau, and Barbusse, because their works depict the inner world and soul of soldiers. And now, in countries such as Germany and Italy, writers are also ordered to write works dedicated to soldiers, which are intended to encourage them—to glorify war or promote militarism. As for countries like Soviet Russia, the publishing industry is even printing soldiers' reading materials on a planned and large scale. Their published "Red Army Library" is indeed quite noteworthy.

Looking back at our China, the situation is completely different. The publishing industry provides almost no assistance to the cultural education of the military. As a result, suitable reading materials for soldiers are extremely rare. Of course, one or two writers who were once young masters or young ladies have written some military diaries, but those are ultimately not understandable to soldiers. It must be known that the only thing that ordinary Chinese soldiers read now is a kind of "Soldier's Daily Lessons." Naturally, this cannot satisfy the soldiers' intellectual desires. But in fact, I have often seen many soldiers secretly reading novels and songbooks on duty. This shows that although most Chinese soldiers are illiterate, everyone has a burning desire for knowledge. If the Chinese publishing industry can imitate the methods of Japanese bookstores and systematically compile several interesting soldiers' reading materials, including basic military textbooks on various military, political, economic, geographical, and natural sciences, I think the sales would definitely be good.

Moreover, because the Chinese military has indeed undergone some reorganization in recent years, and there has been considerable progress in discipline and organization, when forming a national defense force in the future, cultural education will naturally be indispensable. The authorities are now actively carrying out enlightenment education in the military, so objectively, there is a great need for assistance from the publishing industry. This assistance is undoubtedly a very glorious and sacred task for the Chinese publishing industry. Moreover, the publishing industry is currently mired in an atmosphere of recession, suffering from the economic panic. If the publishing industry can truly use part of the financial and human resources used to reprint large numbers of ancient books to assist the cultural education cause in the military, then this would not only be a loyal service to the country, but also open up a new field for the publishing industry itself.

This publication welcomes submissions. Please send them to the Publishing Business Committee of the China Cultural Construction Association at No. 500 Lafayette Road, Shanghai. After publication, we will pay three to four yuan per thousand words.

A Brief Discussion on Literary Translation

— Dezhong

Since the so-called "Eastern Advance of Western Culture," China's seals were opened. European and American guns not only opened China's ports and fortresses, but also opened the eyes of the Chinese people. Everyone opened their eyes to see that foreign countries were not as barbaric and backward as they had imagined, and that there were some things we should learn.

What the eyes could see were only "sound, light, electricity, and chemistry" and "strong ships and powerful guns." Foreign countries only had these material things that we should learn. Thus, the slogan "Chinese learning as the foundation, Western learning for practical use" was born.

At the same time, in the field of literature, there was also a corresponding expression, which was Lin Shu's translations. In the preface to his translation of Haggard's "Allan Quatermain," he said:

"Everywhere it is guided by Lobag as the thread, how is it not very similar to my Sima Qian? ... Observing his focus, he must describe Lobag as the key to the entire chapter, which is the writing method of Sima Qian's Biography of Dawan."

Also, in the preface to his translation of Dickens' "The Old Curiosity Shop," he said:

"I have always said that in ancient texts, narrating everyday and plain matters is the most difficult to write. In Sima Qian's Biographies of the Empresses' Relatives, the description of Bao Changjun said, 'My sister bid me farewell in an inn, begged to wash me, fed me, and then left.' What makes people feel sad is only these few words. ... After all, Sima Qian does not often use this kind of writing, because Sima Qian's book is not specifically about everyday matters. Now Dickens specializes in everyday language, and specializes in writing about the everyday affairs of the lower classes of society, which makes using ink even more difficult."

This very clearly uses "Chinese learning as the foundation, Western learning for practical use" as a banner. Therefore, the reason for translation is still because the original work has places that "resemble my Sima Qian," or that "Sima Qian rarely uses this kind of writing." At that time, this kind of influence spread to various magazines and newspapers, and almost all translations were based on this kind of thought.

The concept of "Chinese learning as the foundation, Western learning for practical use" was eliminated during the May Fourth Movement. In literary translation, it also ushered in a long-term improvement at the same time. First, translation focused on the style of the original work, no longer forcibly incorporating anything from China. Second, in order to maintain the style of the original work, vernacular Chinese was used, and the translation was absolutely faithful.

After this, people were indeed able to work hard according to this new improvement in translation, but apart from a few magazines and translators who could focus on a certain aspect, most translations were still unsystematic and without a purpose. Zheng Zhenduo said:

"We have been introducing European and American literature for thirty or forty years, but we have never had a planned introduction; often, we just grab a book and translate it, or we are constrained by popular ideas, and we often spend a lot of effort translating second- or third-rate works. (World Literature Series)"

These words are a critique of translation over the past three or four decades, and can represent a new understanding of the entire Chinese translation industry.

Accompanied by this kind of understanding, from the second half of last year to the first half of this year, there were three important publications.

The first is "Translation."

In the "Preface" of "Translation," there was no flaunting of any great goals or plans, only saying:

"It is not intended to raise the banner of 'reviving translation'—there is no ambition for this kind of high-pitched call, but just to have a few like-minded people study each other and print it out for people who like to read translations to use as reference."

But if we try to flip through the content of this publication, we can see many works by modern and even contemporary writers, realist or anti-social writers, and works by weak and small peoples.

Although they did not boast much, the content of the publication tells us that it is not just "a few like-minded people studying each other casually."

The second is "World Literature."

In the "Inaugural Statement" of "World Literature," it says:

"In modern Chinese literature, the generalization of form and language is a major problem. In addition, incorporating content into the territory of world literature to establish the direction of Chinese literature, deepen emotions, and enrich appearances is also a major problem. Especially in terms of content, Chinese literature, like other Chinese problems, must be involved in the surging waves of the world to have a considerable solution." It also says:

"This publication is born to strive to fulfill one percent of the thousands of responsibilities in the construction of new literature. Introduce the literature of various countries, estimate its value to world literature, that is, new literature; publish works that can be used in form or content; explore the path of Chinese literature with an absolutely objective attitude. At all times, we hope that this kind of purpose can form a new literary view in China, arousing the attention of the people to new literature."

From the content of this publication, we can see that most of it also pays attention to the works of modern and contemporary writers, but the battle line is not as neat as "Translation," especially in the "Poetry" section.

The previous two publications were all about introducing foreign literature. There is also a third type that publishes half Chinese classics and half foreign works, namely the third: "World Library."

In the "Inaugural Declaration" of "World Library," it says:

"The introduction and recitation of world literary masterpieces is the greatest task (or right) and joy of the people of our time." It also says:

"Our work is to introduce and organize in a planned way, presenting world literary masterpieces to the general readers in the most convenient way."

Judging from the several volumes of "World Library" that have been published, apart from Gogol's "Dead Souls," Cervantes' "Don Quixote," and a few translations by Gorky and Balzac that are needed by modern readers, some translations seem to be fillers, which can only be used as literary history references, and some of them are not even first-rate works. Of course, the publication of "World Library" is intended to introduce ancient and modern masterpieces from abroad and publish Chinese classics as literary history references, and it seems that the needs of the general readers have been completely ignored. But it is too inconvenient for readers to buy so many books that include a lot of unnecessary things in order to read a few articles.

Overall, in the past year, literary translation has indeed had a trend of revival. And the purpose of literary translation is also very different from the past. To sum it up, it can be roughly divided into three aspects: First, at this time, new Chinese literature rarely has very substantial works appearing, and readers have few opportunities to come into contact with foreign literature, so translating foreign literary works to meet these needs of readers is an urgent task. Second, introducing the styles of foreign literary works is for the reference and learning of Chinese authors. Third, literature is universal, and in order to make it a part of world literature, it is necessary to have an understanding of foreign literature.

Although there is now such a progressive understanding and active effort in literary translation, we cannot be too optimistic about it. Many attacks on translation have not stopped for a single day, and the ability of readers to develop interest and need for translated works is still not very widespread.

Now "Translation" has already ceased publication. And according to the "Qingguang" in the "Shishi Xinbao," there are also rumors that "World Literature" will also cease publication. Now there is only one "World Library" that is expensive and not very substantial, and has already been delayed by one issue.

Introducing Three Interesting Mathematics Books

— Qizhong

There is an annoying limerick about mathematics that has been passed down from the European Middle Ages, which roughly says: "Multiplication is annoying, division is also annoying, ratios make people feel helpless, and calculations make people go crazy." Indeed, most people not only don't find mathematics interesting, but also feel a headache when they see it, so the grades of general students are always the worst in mathematics. Even for me personally, more than ten years ago in school, when I encountered a mathematics exam, I always ate tangyuan (a type of dessert, meaning I failed). The mathematics teacher would specially give me twenty points for his own face, and I would accept it without hesitation. There are many people like me in reality, and even if there are differences, they are not very different, so the grades of general students are relatively the worst in mathematics.

Why do most students not like mathematics? Needless to say, this is entirely a matter of interest. The first thing in pursuing any knowledge is to have interest. Without interest, there will never be any achievements. Even with travel, if you are interested in traveling, then even if you climb mountains and wade through water, sweating all over and panting non-stop, you will still feel very happy and soon be able to achieve the goal of "Standing alone on the top of the mountain, I am the peak." On the contrary, for people who have no interest in traveling, forcing them to climb mountains and wade through water will only make them feel pain. Therefore, the most important thing in pursuing knowledge is interest. Because mathematics is a dry and tasteless subject, the grades of general students are also the worst.

Many people think that learning mathematics is only for daily application, but the mathematics learned in schools now completely exceeds daily application. Because it is not suitable for daily application, they feel more and more of a headache when they see dry and abstract mathematics, and their grades become more and more inferior. One day, Euclid's student asked Euclid, "What is the benefit of learning such difficult things?" This question can be said to be generally held by students now for the subject of mathematics, especially a group of middle school students. However, pursuing knowledge is not just for current use. Euclid, in response to his student's question, took out three copper coins from his pocket and replied, "Do you think getting these three copper coins is better than acquiring knowledge?" We must know that mathematics is the foundation for studying science, and we must not be greedy for the three copper coins in front of us and abandon the foundation of science. Therefore, we must not be unenthusiastic about learning mathematics because the mathematics learned in schools is not suitable for daily application.

Most people know the importance of studying science, and most people also know that mathematics is the foundation for studying science. However, knowing the importance of this subject, everyone has to feel a headache for this important subject. Therefore, teachers who teach mathematics must find materials from new aspects to make dry and tasteless things into fresh and interesting materials. This is like bitter medicine, which no one likes to take. Doctors must find a way to infiltrate a sweet taste so that people don't realize they are taking the same medicine. However, so-called textbooks are mostly dry and tasteless things, so what I am introducing here is not textbooks, but mathematics books for general reading. That is, the three books published by Kaiming Bookstore written by Mr. Liu Xunyu: "The Garden of Mathematics" (half a dollar), "Mathematical Interest" (eight jiao), and the "Mathematics and Genius" (six jiao) published in the Middle School Student Magazine.

These three books completely use a rich and interesting style to explain the principles of mathematics, so that readers feel like they are reading an interesting novel, like they are walking into a beautiful garden, making them reluctant to leave. "The Garden of Mathematics" is a relatively systematic explanation of the principles of arithmetic: "Mathematical Interest" is a mathematical article picked up everywhere in daily life: "Mathematics and Genius" is a collection of mathematical articles written by several mathematics experts in interesting language, and the content is similar to "Mathematical Interest." Let's take a look at these topics to see if they are interesting: "Stacking Arhats," "Eight Immortals Crossing the Sea," "Han Xin Counting Soldiers," "Old Man Wang's Soup Dumplings," "If I Had Twelve Fingers"... This is just a part of the topics. There are a total of thirty-nine articles in the three books. After reading these thirty-nine interesting articles, people who feel annoyed by mathematics will definitely develop a great interest in mathematics. Mr. Feng Zikai said: "I have never tasted the interest of mathematics, and I have never visited the world of mathematics, which is a loss." I feel that Mr. Feng's words clearly expressed what was in my heart, and I think there must be many people who feel the same as me!

I don't want to advertise for Kaiming Bookstore and make readers rashly buy these three books. I really hope that readers may first go to the library to borrow these three books—or only borrow one if they can't borrow three—to read. If you read it and it is indeed interesting, then it is not too late to buy it; because the bookstore will never increase the price of the book because the cost of living is becoming more and more expensive day by day.

Comrades who do not feel interested in mathematics (because I am not good at mathematics, and I might as well call people who are like me comrades), please pay attention to my words. If you can arouse your mathematical taste from these three books, it is not only the achievement of the author, but also the good fortune of the comrades!
