Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

Telephone Price Increase and Rent Reduction

— Xin Xin

The Shanghai market has been in a depression in all industries, and has become more and more profound since the Shanghai War (the process and reasons cannot be fully explained in this short article of about a thousand words, so I will omit it for now). Up to now, the four words "economic panic" have not only become a household name, but have also become the slogans of "big sales" and "big bargains." The depth of the panic has been exposed like a patient in the third stage of lung disease, and cannot be concealed.

Accompanying this very blatant form is inevitably the rising call for rent reduction, because for ordinary shops with a monthly business of only one thousand yuan or so, their rent is almost one hundred yuan. Calculated at a profit of 3%, a shop's monthly profit is only about three hundred yuan, and after deducting rent, employee salaries, and other daily expenses, what is the net profit? It has become a problem. Moreover, after the Shanghai War, the business of general shops has to be discounted by at least half, so under the business after the discount, can they afford such high rents? It is already self-evident. The call for rent reduction is very reasonable, and to revive Shanghai and restore it to its previous prosperity, it is necessary to implement rent reduction.

However, after two years of the call for rent reduction, apart from a small number of shops and residents enjoying preferential treatment of 20% or 10% off, the majority are still "nephews holding lanterns"—as usual.

While this rent reduction issue has not yet been resolved, the telephone is about to increase its price according to the new pricing, charging by the number of calls.

In addition to expensive rent, at this time of economic downturn, can citizens still afford even more expensive telephone bills? There is no need for the author to explain, the citizens who are directly affected understand it even better.

However, the fact that rent has not been reduced but telephone bills are increasing is ironclad. Moreover, this ironclad fact will be implemented in the near future.

Although rent reduction is being petitioned to the Sixth Plenary Session, and the telephone price increase is being continuously opposed, according to the Nanjing Road Citizens' Federation, they would rather cut off the telephone lines of the telephone bureau when necessary. However, it is inevitable that the efforts of a single organization will not have good results because they are isolated and weak, and the telephone company authorities are going their own way and insisting to the end.

So, is it to add more weight to a burden that is already suffocating?

Of course not. In order to revive Shanghai, and even more to fight for survival, rent reduction and opposition to the telephone bill increase are not only a matter of rising up in anger and shouting for a while. We must also resolutely take concerted action to implement our demands.

We know that seeking individual gains and demanding as individual units, besides being exploited in an orderly manner, will lead to individual bankruptcy. As a result, apart from being given local anesthesia and temporarily alleviating pain, there will be nothing gained, and it will naturally be even more different from the so-called revival of Shanghai.

Fifty Dollars

— Wen

The dim sunlight climbed over the "Five Sons Pass the Examination" roof ridge, shining on the west-facing windows of these five main rooms. Facing south from the main rooms was a wide courtyard, with two magnolia and osmanthus trees planted in the left and right corners, guarding the main rooms in their shade like two gatekeepers. Facing the main rooms was a high wall, taller than the main building, so passersby outside the wall could not see the "Five Sons Pass the Examination" roof ridge; only bursts of osmanthus fragrance wafted out from the wall, making them cast greedy glances at the top of the high wall.

It was past four in the afternoon, and three or five crows circled the tops of the magnolia trees, but there was still no sound from the main rooms, as if a deserted building was shrouded in deadly silence. The owner of the house was a local gentry, a large landowner, who was being woken from a good dream by his concubine. He—generally called Master Hu, although only a forty-year-old middle-aged man—turned over in his silk quilt, stretched out his yellowish fingers and rubbed his eyes, which were blurred with sleep. He saw his concubine standing in front of the bed with a stern face (because she had called him more than a dozen times, but Master Hu always covered his head with the quilt. Master Hu himself understood this temper; nothing important could wake him up before he was fully awake). He quickly forced an ugly smile and tried to pull the concubine over. But the concubine was like a stone pillar, not at all like she usually was, weakly and

Page 18

easily losing her footing and throwing her upper body into Master Hu's arms with a giggle. Now she tightened her face and slapped away Master Hu's outstretched hand, genuinely angry:

"You can't wake up from your sleep, that Gao...died because of you, see if you..."

She turned her back and slumped into the sofa chair in front of the bed. Master Hu immediately furrowed his bushy eyebrows, but he knew that this was his concubine's jealousy. The day he brought Gao Agen's woman here, they quarreled all night. A jade Buddha more than two feet tall was smashed to pieces by the concubine. Only after he begged and pleaded a thousand times did she calm down. Gao Agen's woman was truly something: she let her hair down, tore her clothes, and tried to kill herself. Even Aunt Liu's silver tongue, which could make the dead speak, was useless! But the concubine was happy instead. She said to Master Hu: "What's so good about that woman? These days, she looks even less like a person. Just let her go back. I heard that Agen had a good early rice harvest. Just bring his grain here!" Master Hu smiled, knowing that the woman, after two days without food, had changed her mind somewhat. He just needed to deceive his concubine's eyes, play with her a bit, and then let her go home; and he wasn't afraid that Agen would welsh on the ninety dollars. Last night, Master Hu secretly went to the secret chamber. The woman was sitting quietly on the bed eating. Aunt Liu whispered in his ear: "There will be a way out in the next two days, Master Hu, don't come. If it goes wrong, Aunt Liu can't bear the responsibility!" She smiled flatteringly and pushed Master Hu out.

Master Hu sat up, leaning against the pillow. He peeked at his concubine's movements through the silk gauze curtain. The concubine had her back to the curtain, and Master Hu knew who had leaked the news about her angry appearance—that woman must have been persuaded by Aunt Liu. Thinking of this, Master Hu's heart bloomed, but he coughed and said softly:

"Why be angry? I don't intend to marry her, just play with her for a while..."

"Hmph!" The concubine jumped up from the sofa: "Don't dream! Who wants to eat this vinegar? Agen hanged himself, and your darling bailiff has been waiting outside the door for more than two hours!" The concubine finally shouted.

Only then did Master Hu jump up. "Is this really the case? Where's A'er?" He grabbed a long robe from the corner of the bed and stepped down.

A'er slipped in from outside the door. He lowered his head, drooped his hands, and didn't know where Master Hu was standing, speaking to the bed: "Master Hu, I went to Agen's house as instructed. He said he would definitely return the fifty dollars from selling the grain and begged me to say good words to the master to let his wife go back. As the master instructed, I couldn't agree... He hanged himself last night..."

"Bastard! Bastard!" Master Hu spun around in the room in his slippers. "You can't even handle this little thing, and you still have the nerve to see me! What happens next? Speak! Speak!"

"They've already reported it to the bureau..." A'er took a few steps back, as if afraid that Master Hu would hit him.

"Hmm!" Master Hu stopped abruptly, his broad eyebrows furrowed, his eyes seemingly spitting sparks. He looked at the concubine standing in front of the bed with her head held high, while A'er retreated to the threshold. Master Hu struck his palm with his fist. "Bastard! Bastard, what are you still standing there for? Quickly take my card to the bureau!" He said to the concubine, "Also, give A'er another fifty dollars. Tell the bureau chief that I'll be there right away!"

"We haven't received the fifty dollars, and we have to spend another fifty dollars?" The concubine sneered.

"What are you saying?!" Master Hu stomped on the floor. "Bastard! Bastard!"

Small Teahouse

— Green Leaves

— Impressions of an Ancient City

On the gray street, only the small teahouse clearly punctuated the gray, lonely atmosphere; a sign painted with golden yellow paint peeled off in patches of gray, its color and tone distinctly gray and lonely.

On one side, water was being sold, the gray wall and gray stove basking in the bright sunlight. Usually, one or two women and children, carrying copper kettles, would come to buy water. As the copper coins clinked lonesomely in the bamboo container, a tall man, always wearing the same ordinary expression, would scoop a kettle of hot water for them and silently put the ladle away. He stood listlessly by the stove, listening to the interesting gossip of the townspeople, or adding some coal to the stove. Sometimes, when he met the women, he would also knowingly strike up a conversation and flirt with them.

On that gray pillar, a faded red strip of paper was pasted, on which the words "Hairdressing" were written in large, red-filled characters. Sometimes, we could see the red strip of paper fluttering quietly in the wind; beneath it was a young lad with a white cloth skirt tied around his chest, smeared with many streaks of snot, straight and crooked—he was a barber. He was a lonely one, wasn't he? We could see his pair of eyes stealthily sizing up the beauty of the woman buying water.

The mouths and eyes of many of the teahouse's patrons were perhaps forever gray and lonely; they added gray material and gray loneliness to the small teahouse. Each of them longed for the beauty of Jiangnan and the famous city of Shanghai, harboring in the depths of their hearts this kind of beautiful gold mine, and base hopes.

Most of the customers in this teahouse were small merchants of the "chicken-stealing-for-feathers" variety, and there were also one or two vagrants and crude, tall rickshaw pullers. Every day, they let gray and lonely years slip away in the gray and lonely small teahouse. They talked about women's jokes and town gossip—when talking about women interestingly, they would laugh basely. Sometimes, when they heard town gossip that was as absurd as a myth, everyone would ask and talk about it with concern, the crude laughter of the rickshaw pullers punctuating the surroundings.

Here, the rickshaw pullers were the most straightforward and crude; they would never hide an interesting word in their hearts; they would say in low, soft voices the interesting stories of their women, adding to the laughter. In their—the rickshaw pullers'—hearts, there was only a glimmer of warm comfort.

Every day, they bore their resentment, growing up in the gray world and the gray ancient city. One vagrant would say that the gray loneliness of this ancient city would eat away at their lives and their spirits, so they all longed for the beautiful watery towns of distant Jiangnan and the bustling Shanghai. Only this was their most colorful, rich, and complex topic of conversation. They envied the luxury of Shanghai, and at the same time hoped to visit Shanghai or Jiangnan for half a year. In a gray life, people need a little bit of warmth.

Every day, they talked about the sights of Shanghai, and that knowledgeable, flat-faced, short waiter would agree in a low voice, his wide eyes longing for Shanghai. At dusk, customers would stream out onto the gray streets and alleys, returning to their gray homes. In the small teahouse, only the lonely waiter was left, tidying up the messy tea trays on the tables, and the boiling water on the stove hissed in loneliness.

The Temptation of Purple Grapes

— Chen Liang

This is a small, rustic garden, with poplars, maple trees, ginkgos, secluded paths paved with green stones, and grape trellises made of pine branches. Every day, when a soft ray of late autumn sunset shines on the vermillion railing of the third floor of the Wen Kui Pavilion, I would have a collection of poetry, a few mild cigarettes, and a leisurely mood, strolling by the small pond filled with wild vegetables and dodder vines.

Here, I am not subjected to the temptation of lust or the threat of wealth. I can indulge in all private fantasies and freely conjure up some past memories, whether sweet, bitter, or as bitter as coptis, I always consider it a kind of stimulation, letting my numb life tremble once. Occasionally, I can also lean against the cool rocks of the artificial hill and sing a mournful tune. The autumn clouds are faint, and human feelings are also faint. I really don't know how many times my enthusiasm and tearful grievances have been deceived by hypocrisy. Now, I pity this physiological secretion.

The grass and trees, caressed by the seasonal winds, appear even more decadent and old. Poplars shed a pond full of hair, maple trees flushed red in the face, and the old sycamore leaves kept rolling on the garden path. Ah, I watched them sprout, I watched them shield people from the scorching sun in the summer, and now, I see them wither, wither, how fast! This process seems to only go from morning to night! What about the men and women who used to sit under their thick shade, whispering sweet nothings? I want to find them back, let them lean again under the decaying branches and sigh to each other.

At this time, I can't help but feel a sense of sorrow about the emptiness of living things. I need the comfort of some fruits. The male ginkgo doesn't bear fruit, and a scorched leaf sticks to the spider web under the eaves, whistling softly in the cool autumn wind. This sound seems so hollow. I always visit this garden with an empty mind, looking for fruits, but there are none, none... The brown seeds of the dodder have also burst and been buried in the soil.

The day before yesterday, the day before yesterday was an unexpected discovery. When I was smoking a mild cigarette, sitting under the grape trellis, I suddenly felt a temptation. A bunch of purple grapes was half-hidden in the scorched yellow leaves. I counted, one, two, three... crowded together in clusters, so many that I couldn't count them all. I examined them carefully, and there was another bunch over there, and another bunch over there, bunches and bunches of purple, translucent berries. Isn't this the rich fruit of late autumn? How can this small garden be empty!

That night, I had a wonderful dream: every corner of the world contains fulfilling components, and every branch of life hangs with ripe fruits, just waiting for people to discover, seek, and indulge in their desired sweetness. ...

(Indeed, everything in the world contains temptations as crystal-clear and radiant as purple grapes, especially when they are about to ripen. But people are too impatient to pick and swallow those unripe, green, and sour fruits. Therefore, people have two kinds of lament: lamenting that in life, they only tasted the frowning sourness, and lamenting that in the season of truly ripe fruits, they can't find a large quantity of sweet fruits to satisfy their desires. Therefore, the former is disappointment, and the latter is also disappointment.)

However, am I a patient person? Before discovering the purple grapes ripening on the trellis, I always thought that this small, rustic garden was empty.

Radio Broadcast

Song Introduction

Song of the Night Moon

The night is deep, people are quiet, the wind is soft, the stars are bright. Half a cloud covers the bright and radiant moon completely. A scene of dim twilight displeases everyone. Let us strive for our future! Uncover the white clouds, let the bright, pure, and spotless moon burst out of the white clouds, illuminating the darkness of the world and creating light from despair. We do not want the moon to wane, we do not want the moon to sink, we wish the moon in the sky will always be brightly radiant, radiant and bright.

The night is long, the insects are chirping, the wind is rustling, the stars are twinkling. Floating clouds cover the bright and radiant moon completely. A scene of lonely tranquility saddens everyone. Let us rouse our spirits! Open up the floating clouds, let the clear, delicate, and round moon surge out of the floating clouds, illuminating the darkness of the world and creating light from despair. We do not want the moon to wane, we do not want the moon to sink, we wish the moon in the sky will always be brightly radiant, radiant and bright.

Storytelling Ballad

Xia Hesheng's Three Smiles

Dun Ben (800) 7:00 PM to 8:00 PM

Opening "Su Qin"

Unsuccessful Su Qin humiliated and ashamed. Burst into anger in his heart. He hated his parents for not acknowledging their own son. His brother was ruthless and would not let him stay. His wife was unwilling to lower the loom. All affection as husband and wife was abandoned. If I had known this day, I would have been greatly deceived. I regret not shaving my head and becoming a monk. Without worries or concerns, why pursue riches and honor? Flesh and blood are like strangers. Married couples are like enemies. What use is this life? It would be better to die and end all things. He looked into the well with both hands. Life seemed very insignificant. He was about to throw himself into the well when his uncle grabbed his clothes. Could it be that fame and fortune are difficult to obtain? Quickly tell me the reason. I presented a ten-thousand-word memorial. But it was opposed by Shang Yang. He was unwilling to present my request to the king. Crestfallen, I returned home ashamed. Just now, I went home. My family was heartless and unwilling to let me stay. Causing me to feel anger and have no way to vent. I would rather end my life by jumping into the well. Ah, my son, fame and fortune are determined by fate. How can wealth and honor be easily obtained? If you don't pass the imperial examination this time, there will be another time to pass. Don't be so short-sighted. Quickly go home with me. Bury yourself in your studies by the window. Uncle, I am grateful for your help. If I go to my aunt, she will surely take me in. Read ten thousand volumes of ancient books. Fame and fortune will come easily without worry. Su Qin had no choice but to follow his uncle home. Later, he was granted nobility by the six states. At that time, he returned in triumph.

Xing Ruiting's Hairpin Phoenix

Huiling (1380) 9:00 PM to 10:00 PM

Opening "West Chamber"

Apricot blossoms ten miles red. Miss Yingying in the room. Only for Zhang Junrui of the West Chamber. Too lazy to embroider in the boudoir. Yesterday, Hongniang went to the West Chamber. She said that Zhang Xiang Gong was sick in bed. I wanted to go and see him. But I am afraid of my mother's family rules. I had no choice but to write a letter to Zhang Junrui. Don't hang me in your heart. I immediately took out the writing tools. My slender fingers ground the ink. Gently writing the letter. Drawing the flower seal over and over. Then she cut off her fragrant hair. Wrapped with red and green velvet. She told Hongniang to take the letter to Zhang Xiang Gong. Hongniang obeyed the order. She passed through the corridors and turned east. Entering the two purple bamboo doors. All she saw was that the flowers and trees in the garden were brightly colored. Flowers and stones lined up in a chessboard pattern. Roses were woven into brocade screens. Happily, white cranes and crabapple trees were planted along the street. The old plum trees were very delicate. Banana trees were planted on the east side. Large phoenix trees on the west side. Thousand-year bamboo and pines faced each other. Red Niang was walking alone across the Shouxian Bridge. All she saw was the small bridge and flowing water. On the east side of the bridge were willows. Lotuses had not yet turned red in the pond. Mandarin ducks were embracing each other by the pond. Golden fish transformed into dragons in the lake. Hongniang was. Then she walked under the wisteria trellis. All she saw were hydrangeas facing her. She turned into the Peach Blossom Cave. Inside the Immortal Cave was the Old Man Peak. Enjoying the night scene in the Moon Gazing Pavilion. Rabbits often played in the grass. All she saw was the Mandarin Duck Hall built ingeniously. Chicken crowns, young and old, were planted by the rockery. She saw a study facing south. The furnishings were very exquisite inside. In the center was a rosewood table. Six fine plum stools on both sides. Mica screens were placed facing outwards. The God of Literature was enshrined in the center. Incense was burned in a bronze censer. Quickly descending, the incense smoke penetrated nine layers of clouds. A famous painting hung in the center. The brushwork was delicate and fine. A pair of couplets was on both sides. Silk-edged, rice paper red. The first line was, the wind blows the willow branches in lines. The second line was, the rain hits the peach blossoms in petals. She could not finish seeing all the sights of the study. She had already arrived at the inner room. She walked to the bed and stood still. She saw a scholar half-asleep. He was panting and leaning against a mandarin duck pillow. There was no page nearby. "Xiang Gong, I have been ordered to deliver a letter." Zhang Sheng heard and smiled. He took the letter and immediately opened it. Carefully reading it from beginning to end. The writing inside was very affectionate. Since that visit to the Puji Temple. Our hearts have been in love. That year, the bandits caused chaos. My mother betrothed me to my brother. You exerted yourself to repel the soldiers. You were a heroic white horse general. Unexpectedly, my mother suddenly regretted the marriage. I heard you were full of hatred. I urge you to take care of yourself first. Do not hang me in your heart. Wait until the Mid-Autumn Festival in August. I will send Hongniang to deliver a letter again. I will tell you my love under the moon.

Movie News

Tianyi's Colorful Records

Tianyi's new sound film "Mother" is led by Wen Yimin, written by Wang Bin, and stars Fan Xuepeng, Zuo Ming, Zhang Zhengfan, Yu Guang, Chen Jingfang, Liang Wenyuan, etc. It will be released soon at the Jincheng Grand Theater in Shanghai.

The 20,000 copies of the third printing of the "Mother" song sheet music have also been given away. It is said that over 30,000 copies have been given to all 2,000+ large, medium, and small schools in Shanghai. The fourth edition has already been printed, and those who want the sheet music can still send in requests.

The "Mother" special issue is exquisitely printed by the Commercial Press. The content is exceptionally rich and includes works by Mr. Hong Shen, Ying Yunwei, Zuo Ming, Wen Yimin, Gu Jianchen, Shi Pengnian, Wu Yun, Mei Zhi, and others.

The main idea of Tianyi's new film "Welcoming Spring Song" is to explain that the life of workers is painful, and at the same time, it also explains that the life of capitalists is also painful.

Hong Shen's "Flowers and Grass," which was written for Tianyi, is said to have passed the preliminary review.

"Welcoming Spring Song" and "Flowers and Grass" will start filming one after another. The cast has not yet been announced.

Tianyi's new sound film "Two Brothers" will be released after "Mother."

Leng Bo recently wrote a script for Tianyi, titled "Enemies."

The rumor that Camera Man Shen Yongshi left Tianyi is false.

"All-China Games Newsreel" has been printed with five sample films and sent to various places.

The theme song of "Sea Burial" has now been translated into simplified notation by the original author, Mr. Zhang Hao, for the purpose of printing and giving it away to all sectors.

Since the Mingxing Film Company began screening films related to the "Jade Horse" giveaway campaign, requests have been overwhelming, reaching several thousand copies daily.
